href="/wiki/File:Truro_stmarysst.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Truro_stmarysst.jpg/220px-Truro_stmarysst.jpg" width="220" height="296" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Truro_stmarysst.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Truro Cathedral from St Mary\'s Street</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Diocese of Truro</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> diocese in the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canterbury" title="Province of Canterbury">Province of Canterbury</a> which covers <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a> and a small part of <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_history">Geography and history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography and history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Cornwall" title="Christianity in Cornwall">Christianity in Cornwall</a></div>\n<p>The diocese\'s area is that of the county of Cornwall, including the Isles of Scilly, as well as two <a href="/wiki/Parish" title="Parish">parishes</a> in neighbouring Devon (<a href="/wiki/St_Giles_on_the_Heath" title="St Giles on the Heath">St Giles on the Heath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginstow" title="Virginstow">Virginstow</a>). It was formed on 15 December 1876 from the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Archdeacons_of_Cornwall" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Archdeacons of Cornwall">Archdeaconry of Cornwall</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Exeter" title="Diocese of Exeter">Diocese of Exeter</a>. It is, therefore, one of the younger dioceses.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The Christian faith, however, has been present in the region since at least the 4th century \xe2\x80\x93 more than 100 years before there was an Archbishop of Canterbury. Many of the communities in the diocese, as well as the parish churches, bear a Celtic saint\'s name, which is a reminder of the links with other Celtic lands, especially Ireland, Wales and Brittany.\n</p><p>The Diocese of Truro is involved directly and indirectly through its Board of Social Responsibility and in the life of its parishes in tackling some of the economic problems that Cornwall is wrestling with and works closely with statutory and voluntary agencies. There are 313 church buildings.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bishops">Bishops</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Bishops">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The diocesan See is vacant; in August 2018, Philip Mounstephen was announced as the 16th bishop of Truro.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Goldsmith" title="Chris Goldsmith">Chris Goldsmith</a>, the suffragan <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_St_Germans" title="Bishop of St Germans">Bishop of St Germans</a> (which see was created in 1905) is acting diocesan bishop of Truro. At some periods there have also been assistant bishops, including John Wellington (formerly Bishop of <a href="/wiki/Shantung" class="mw-redirect" title="Shantung">Shantung</a>) and <a href="/wiki/William_Quinlan_Lash" class="mw-redirect" title="William Quinlan Lash">Bill Lash</a>, both retired from Sees abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Provincial_episcopal_visitor" title="Provincial episcopal visitor">provincial episcopal visitor</a> for parishes in the diocese, among twelve other dioceses in the western part of the Province of Canterbury, which do not accept the ministry of women priests, is <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Goodall" title="Jonathan Goodall">Jonathan Goodall</a>, the suffragan <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Ebbsfleet" title="Bishop of Ebbsfleet">Bishop of Ebbsfleet</a>. He is licensed as an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_assistant_bishop" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary assistant bishop">honorary assistant bishop</a> of the diocese in order to facilitate his ministry.\n</p><p>The most recent suffragan <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Plymouth_(Anglican)" title="Bishop of Plymouth (Anglican)">Bishop of Plymouth</a> in the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Exeter" title="Diocese of Exeter">Diocese of Exeter</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Ford_(bishop)" title="John Ford (bishop)">John Ford</a>, was also licensed as an honorary assistant bishop in Truro diocese.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> A former Bishop of St Germans, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Screech" title="Roy Screech">Roy Screech</a>, lives in <a href="/wiki/St_Austell" title="St Austell">St Austell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archdeaconries_and_deaneries">Archdeaconries and deaneries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a colspan="3"><b>Total/average</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>91</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>305</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>535,272</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>5,882</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>1,755</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>3.35</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rural_deaneries">Rural deaneries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rural deaneries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The names of the older deaneries (before 1875) are based on those of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Hundreds_of_Cornwall" title="Hundreds of Cornwall">Hundreds of Cornwall</a> though the boundaries do not always correspond. East and West (Wivelshire) must have originally had a Cornish name but it is not recorded (Wivel may be from an Anglo-Saxon personal name \'Wifel\').<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The deaneries created in 1875 in the episcopate of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Temple" title="Frederick Temple">Frederick Temple</a> were Bodmin, Stratton, St Austell and Carnmarth. These remained unchanged until Carnmarth was divided; later still in the 1980s some alterations of boundaries occurred. The need for smaller deaneries was caused by the economic growth of Victorian Cornwall, mainly in tin and copper mining, which increased the population and by a greater effort by the church to encourage church membership.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg/150px-C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg.png" width="150" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg/225px-C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg/300px-C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="641" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:C_of_E_Diocese_of_Truro.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coat of arms of the Diocese of Truro</div></div></div>\n<p>The arms of the diocese include a saltire gules on which are a crossed sword and key: below this is a <i>fleur de lys</i> sable, all surrounded by a border sable charged with 15 bezants. The saltire is the cross of St Patrick, taken to be the emblem of the Celtic church; the sword and key are emblems of Ss Peter and Paul, the patrons of <a href="/wiki/Exeter_Cathedral" title="Exeter Cathedral">Exeter Cathedral</a>, and the <i>fleur de lys</i> represents St Mary, patron of the cathedral. The border is derived from the arms of the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">Duchy of Cornwall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> They were designed by the College of Heralds in 1877 and are blazoned thus:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>"Argent, on a saltire gules, a key, ward upward, in bend, surmounted by a sword, hilt upward, in bend sinister, both or. In base, a fleur de lys sable. The whole within a bordure sable, fifteen bezants. Ensigned with a mitre."<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2003 a campaign group was formed called <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fry_an_Spyrys&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fry an Spyrys (page does not exist)">Fry an Spyrys</a></i> ("Free the Spirit" in Cornish) which is dedicated to disestablishing the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> in Cornwall and to reconstituting the Diocese of Truro as an autonomous province of the Anglican Communion. Its most vociferous member is the founder, the Revd Andy Phillips, who also writes under the pen-name "An Bucca". Its chairman is <a href="/wiki/Garry_Tregidga" title="Garry Tregidga">Garry Tregidga</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Cornish_Studies" title="Institute of Cornish Studies">Institute of Cornish Studies</a>. Phillips states there has been constant speculation that the diocese might be merged back into the Diocese of Exeter for budgetary reasons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The possibility of a merger was aired unofficially in March 2003, during debate surrounding the formulation of the Dioceses, Pastoral and Mission Measure, which would allow diocesan commissions to make proposals for the reorganisation of dioceses, including their dissolution. However, such a merger has yet to be proposed by any official body within the Church of England. When the possibility was raised by <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fry_an_Spyrys&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fry an Spyrys (page does not exist)">Fry an Spyrys</a></i> in 2004 it was denied by a Church of England spokesman and also by representatives of the Truro and Exeter dioceses<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Since then the Diocese of Truro has shown some financial and administrative resilience. Diocesan reorganisation and the People of God campaign rallied human resources and led (by 2007) to a tight but stable financial situation. More recently <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lloyd_of_Berwick" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Lloyd of Berwick">Lord Lloyd of Berwick</a>, who chairs Parliament\'s Ecclesiastical Committee, reported to the House of Lords that there are no plans to abolish the Diocese of Truro and to merge it with the Diocese of Exeter.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jeremy_Dowling_Review">Jeremy Dowling Review</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Jeremy Dowling Review">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A 2018 <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.trurodiocese.org.uk/wp-content/uploads/2018/05/JD-Review-Final-May-25-2018-DOT.pdf">case review</a> commissioned by the diocese reported that four bishops, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Key" title="Maurice Key">Maurice Key</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Mumford" title="Peter Mumford">Peter Mumford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ball_(bishop)" title="Michael Ball (bishop)">Michael Ball</a><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Llewellin" title="Richard Llewellin">Richard Llewellin</a>, had failed to respond to disclosures of abuse by a leading diocesan figure. The diocese had failed to investigate the accusations against Jeremy Dowling, a lay preacher and Synod member, who rose to influential positions including communications officer to the bishop. Dowling was jailed in 2015 for seven years, and again in 2016 for a further eight years, for a series of indecent assaults on boys while teaching at a Cornwall school during the 1960s and 70s. Professor Kim Stevenson, a criminal justice expert said the report made \xe2\x80\x9csadly familiar reading\xe2\x80\x9d and she contrasted the situation in Britain with that in Australia where those who concealed or did not act on evidence of a sexual offence faced prosecution.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_churches_in_the_diocese">List of churches in the diocese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Diocese_of_Truro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: List of churches in the diocese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Grade I: buildings of exceptional interest.\nGrade II*: particularly important buildings of more than special interest.\nGrade II: buildings that are of special interest, warranting every effort to preserve them.\n</p><p><i>Last fully updated 26 September 2018.</i>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Deanery_of_Stratton_.5B1.5D"></span><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="425">Benefice\n</th>\n<th>Churches</th>\n<th>Link\n</th>\n<th>Clergy\n</th>\n<th>Population served\n</th>\n<th>Ref\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boyton,_Cornwall" title="Boyton, Cornwall">Boyton</a> (Holy Name), <a href="/wiki/North_Tamerton" title="North Tamerton">North
